0060555661|4.0|After reading the intelligent investor, I can now say that I understand what it takes to truly understand the securities that I purchase for my portfolio. The book does a fantastic job of opening a basic investor's eyes to the fact that the focus of investing is to stay with the market, not to greatly outperform it.<br /><br />The Intelligent Investor is a very in depth and dense book that looks at many different aspects of investing. I would not suggest this book for a relatively new investor who does not have much knowledge on the terminology of investing. However for someone that has had severe losses or struggles with diversifying their portfolio, I feel that this book is a fantastic fit.<br /><br />The book starts off by discussing what exactly an \\"intelligent investor\\" is and the difference between a defensive/conservative investor and one that has sufficient amounts of time to spend towards investing. It continues by laying the groundwork for what an investor should be looking for as well as what they should be looking to avoid. The book also paints a phenomenal picture of the market as a whole with sufficient information on its history and what can be learned from its history. The book continues on by laying out exactly what types of securities different investors should be looking for and how their portfolio should be split amongst these securities. Graham also focuses a fair amount of time on informing the reader of what type of investments they should be avoiding and why. He mentions that the aggressive investor should \\"avoid inferior types of bonds and preferred stocks unless they can be bought at bargain levels\\" and should \\"leave high-grade preferred stocks to corporate buyers\\". Graham also allocates some time to discussing the resources that are available to investors including investment advisers. He does not say that he is completely against the idea of an adviser but that it is crucial to find an adviser that is a good fit for an investor and maintains the same ideals of investing as him. The book then goes into specific examples of security analysis which truly help lay out the ideas that Graham is trying to push. There are many examples including a top down analysis of four different stocks as well as a comparison on different pairs of stocks and which ones would fit the ideas of the intelligent investor. The book then concludes with the fact that time needs to be spent not just on researching the stock, but also as a shareholder of the company. One must be confident in the management team that has control of their money. The last part of the book concludes with the fact that an intelligent investor is not really looking to make it big, but is looking to be comfortable with their portfolio. Hence Graham really pushes the fact that investors can not just follow the masses, but instead must take a step back and look at the market as a whole to understand exactly where it may be going next.<br /><br />The style of the book is very unconventional from many books that I have read. It provides commentary from Jason Zweig who essentially interprets the teaching of Graham into today's world. There are also many footnotes throughout the book which tend to get the reader a little off track simply by the fact that the footnotes tend to be full of information as well. Hence a reader may feel that they are jumping from idea to idea while reading the book. For me, the most helpful way to read the book is summarizing what was just read in a chapter and documenting this knowledge somewhere. Otherwise the reader may get lost in the transitions from chapter to chapter and what exactly is trying to be taught next.  However, in my opinion the structure of the book and the commentary provided does truly help portray the ideals of Benjamin Graham and brings them up to date with current examples.<br /><br />For me, the most useful parts of the book were the first five chapters and the last six chapters. The first part of the bookreally laid out a solid definition of exactly what the book was trying to teach and what type of investing strategy it would be focusing on. If one is looking to have high risk in their portfolio and large amounts of volatility, then this book is definitely not for you. However, being at a young age, the book has given me the confidence to go into the market and become an investor in my future because of the fact that there is much time that lies ahead of me. Graham says that \\"the rate of return sought should be dependent, rather, on the amount of intelligent effort the investor is willing able to bring to bear on his task.\\" The end of the book is where the entire real world examples actually come into play and show exactly what type of analysis needs to be performed on stocks. By having both examples from the time of Graham as well as more current examples from the commentary, one is able to get a full scope of the strategy that Graham is preaching. However it is clear that in order to truly become a master of intelligent investing, one needs to dedicate a lot of time and practice.<br /><br />Overall, the book truly paints a very broad picture with regards to investing. It does not state that one should allocate a specific percentage of their money to stocks, mutual funds, bonds, etc. Rather it teaches the reader how they should go about looking for securities to invest in. The book also shows the benefits of getting a dividend, how to access and read earnings reports, what to look for in these reports, and how to perform a side by side comparison of different investment opportunities. As mentioned throughout this review, the book does not tell you what to do but rather shows you should you should be doing. Do not expect to get a clear cut answer of what to be investing in after reading this book. Instead, one should expect to know how to efficiently utilize their time to analyze different stocks and prepare for what the market may do to their portfolio.<br /><br />As a reader of this book, I feel that the most beneficial next step that can be taken is looking into classes offered by brokerage firms that teach them how to utilize the tools they offer. I would suggest avoiding classes that teach you to invest, and rather focus more on classes that teach you how to utilize the tools provided. Overall, I have truly enjoyed this book and feel that I will definitely read it again because there is still much that this book has to offer.

B009A882D0|4.0|As a band whose albums, singles and live performances were equally exciting, it can be argued that Creedence Clearwater Revival remains the greatest group in American rock `n' roll history. Whether stretching out a psychedelic jam of \\"Suzie Q\\" or \\"I Heard it Through the Grapevine,\\" or packing everything they had into the 2:21 of \\"Bad Moon Rising,\\" their synthesis of rock, country, blues, and southern soul was riveting. Their hit singles still leave listeners reaching to turn up the volume, and their albums harbor dozens of lesser-known, but no less terrific covers and Fogerty originals. In a six-album stretch from 1968's eponymous [[ASIN:B001AKTZP0 Creedence Clearwater Revival]] through 1970's [[ASIN:B001AKTZOG Pendulum]], the quartet never faltered - dropping dozens of hit singles and revitalizing well-selected covers with iconic guitar riffs and vocal turns that hook your ear as readily today as they did forty years ago.<br /><br />The CCR catalog has seen its fair share of reissues, with a [[ASIN:B00005OM4K box set]] in 2001, individual album remasters in 2008, and in 2009 a mono [[ASIN:B002W0GN20 singles collection]], vintage [[ASIN:B000000XBX live concert]] and a [[ASIN:B001YXXS8S covers collection]]. And then there are numerous tributes and an endless array of karaoke discs. Fantasy's latest reiteration of the core catalog is a three-disc set that goes beyond the hit singles, but not as far as the box set. It's a better introduction than a single disc, and with the inclusion of album and live tracks, a broader look than the two volume Chronicle set. The set is delivered in a tri-fold cardboard sleeve with extensive liner notes by Bay Area music historian, Alec Palao. Among his insights is the astonishing fact that CCR never scored a chart-topping U.S. single; [[ASIN:B001AKTZPA Green River]] and [[ASIN:B0045FTQJW Cosmo's Factory]] each topped the album chart, but their peak singles, \\"Proud Mary,\\" \\"Green River\\" and \\"Lookin' Out My Back Door\\" topped out at #2.<br /><br />Perhaps it's fitting that the longevity of the group's legacy is broader than hit singles. The set's first two discs sample from the group's seven original studio albums, including four Fogerty-piloted tracks from the swansong, [[ASIN:B000000XCM Mardi Gras]]. Disc three collects live performances from 1970-71, recorded in the Bay Area and across Europe; all were previously issued on either [[ASIN:B000000XBX The Concert]] or as bonus tracks to the 2008 album reissues. The live mixes are necessarily rawer than the studio recordings, but they're full and punchy, show off the band's tight ensemble playing and demonstrate how well CCR's material translated to the stage. This is a great set for listeners who haven't upgraded their Chronicle LPs to CDs, those not ready for the box or album reissues, or younger listeners that need to have the waxy buildup of contemporary pop removed from their ears. 0547884591|5.0|The 4-Hour Chef is the latest and greatest from Tim Ferriss. As an avid reader of his previous two books, I have to admit that I approached the new book with a cautious optimism. Having now read it, I can officially remove that \\"cautious\\" label: not only is the book a fascinating take on the intersection of two worlds (learning and cooking), but it is also gorgeously designed cover-to-cover and chalk full of practical lessons for even the most stubbornly-awful chefs-in-the-making.<br /><br />The book opens with a discussion on meta-learning, or learning how to learn. In this, Tim discusses methods from the world's top learners, and outlines his method for absorbing information rapidly. It then flows into \\"The Domestic,\\" which is the idiot's guide to cooking - the items every kitchen needs, the most efficient way to stock your pantry, and early lessons for some easy, but impressive dishes. From there, the book takes a turn for the outdoorsy with \\"Wild,\\" where Tim covers his first hunt, how to make drinkable water, and all sorts of fun Les Stroud-esque material. The following chapter, \\"The Scientist\\" includes the brainier side of cooking - from bacon infusing your bourbon to making \\"crunchy\\" bloody mary's - and the science behind each recipe. The book closes with \\"Pro\\" - an analysis of the world's top restaurants and a few easy favorites to take your cooking skills to the next level.<br /><br />Usually it takes months after reading a book for it to form any practical implementation in my life, no matter how profound the content. The 4-Hour Chef's turnaround time is sitting at just over a day. On a Thanksgiving trip home, it was time to impress the parents by showing off my newfound cooking chops. I gathered up a few ingredients, got my meez (mise-en-place) all ready, and fired up the Dutch oven. A couple hours (and a number of \\"mmm... something smells good\\"! comments) later, I happily served up a nice plate of Osso \\"Buko\\" (Tim's take on the modern classic) and coconutcauliflower curry mash - two of the first recipes in the book. It was fantastic - the best meal I've cooked in years - and made me look like a cooking virtuoso. I was welcomed with choruses of \\"wow, thanks so much for dinner!\\" from the parents. I shrugged my shoulders and received the compliments with open arms. In reality, I have just one person to thank: Tim.

To be able to actually see how she had incorporated the various stitches/techniques into her work was so useful.  I usually skip the project sections in books, but I found that even here, Eakin had included more helpful suggestions.  Eakin's design sense is lovely and very different from that of a Sheri Serafini or Heidi Kumli, which is interesting in and of itself.  The wide variety of designs and the numerous photographs were excellent and inspirational, as well as practical.  This is like a Master Class for bead embroidery and will work well for beginners as well as experienced bead embroiderers. It is definitely a \\"go to\\" book and will undoubtedly become the textbook for beaders.  It makes you want to pick up your needle and get going.

0062183591|4.0|It is no surprise that dishonesty exists in abundance.  The early economic work on dishonesty considered it a rational calculation based off cost/benefit analysis which fits nicely into pre-existing models for human behaviour for economists.  Subsequent experimental work has shown this to be inaccurate and failing in many dimensions.  Dan Ariely i a behavioural economist and uses The Honest Truth About Dishonesty as a means to discuss in various contexts how we can be dishonest, how we justify it to ourselves and how the environment impacts out decision making.  Some of it is quite intuitive, but much of the book is enlightening and provocative.  I'll give a quick overview of the contents.<br /><br />The rational crime model, as mentioned above, was the first model of crime being a result of rational computing of the cost benefit of committing the crime.  The author first discusses examples which contradict the pure conclusions of such cost benefit analysis for example using examples of cab driver fairs for the blind versus those with sight (the rational outcome would favor those with sight to get a shorter route, but it turns out the opposite is true).  Other examples like white collar crime and the magnitude of cheating in experiments where one is not observed cheating are discussed (in experiments where the monetary reward increased the magnitude of cheating remained the same in many examples showing that cheating was not based off the risk reward in any pure sense).  The author continues on with many more examples of cheating that we can rationalize and how we exaggerate the cheating of others.  Golf and the readjustment of the ball is discussed (with using a club being much more self justifiable means to move the ball than picking up and moving the ball with ones hand for a bad lie).  How the mulligan is typically used on the first hole as one can easier rationalize that the game has not started on the first hole than a subsequent.  The author goes on to discuss how our personal incentives can often cloud our professional judgement- for example the use of medical equipment post the purchase to justify the purchase rather than objectively judging each case for such medical equipment.  The author discusses how fatigue affects our honesty and how concentration and resisting temptation just sets us up to fall for it shortly thereafter by wearing us down mentally.  The author also looks at the subject of fake goods (ie designer goods).  The show how the wearing of fake goods increases the ability to be dishonest on disassociated tests, indicating breaking small ethical codes can impact aggregate behaviour by shifting ones moral compass.  The author analysis how we can convince ourselves that we are better than we are at testing when the solutions are subtely within sight.  Probably one of the more contentious parts of the book is about how creative people are better at lying.  The study was done on people with more white matter in a certain part of the brain which is the connective tissue among neurons- the argument being those who can use a wider range of reasons can more easily rationalize their behaviour and that ability to aggregate the larger range experience and knowledge is where creativity comes from.  Essentially was shown that creative people have greater ability to rationalize their bad behaviour through creative story telling and self delusion.  Definitely an interesting idea.  The author then discusses how cheating and dishonest behaviour can propogate as a function of the environment and whether the behaviour is legitimate in the eyes of the group thus discussing how much is cheating a function of social norms vs internal moral compass.  Interesting experiments show how much whether cheating is done inside or outside the group impacts its influence on the groups behaviour.  FInally the author discusses how cheating emerges in collaborative groups in which catering to peers is balanced by the individuals in the group.<br /><br />All the experiments included are good food for thought about how people can act in various situations and how they justify their behaviour.  The author is quick to point out that rationally we would all cheat and be dishonest more if it were a rational calculation so our nature is quite collaborative and based on reciprocity.  He also throughout the book shows how certain principles help keep us in line (repeating honor codes, asking ourselves whether we would be acting differently if our peers were watching etc...) and such basic guidelines will be useful in helping us keep ourselves more in line passively.  Much is intuitive in the book, but the way the information i put together makes it very enjoyable to read and informative as well, definitely recommended.oup.<br /><br />All the experiments included are good food for thought about how people can act in various situations and how they justify their behaviour.  The author is quick to point out that rationally we would all cheat and be dishonest more if it were a rational calculation so our nature is quite collaborative and based on reciprocity.  He also throughout the book shows how certain principles help keep us in line (repeating honor codes, asking ourselves whether we would be acting differently if our peers were watching etc...) and such basic guidelines will be useful in helping us keep ourselves more in line passively.  Much is intuitive in the book, but the way the information i put together makes it very enjoyable to read and informative as well, definitely recommended.

1840221828|5.0|I am one who resonates deeply with the kind of themes that Kafka treats in his works: bureaucracy, meaning, connection, relationships, and how hierarchy impacts the way we experience and sit in the world. This is an unfinished novel--this is true. But if  you have read any Kafka, I you probably understand that this plain simple truth should not deter a venture into the text. In fact, the mid-sentence ends in just the right spot--it leaves the reader with the resounding feeling that in fact the feeling you've been having the entire book--namely that K, the main character, is forever stuck in a maze of absurd bureaucratic run-arounds--is how life for K will be for the indefinite future. There is no major epiphany. No breakthrough that makes the previous 270 pages feel as if they were actually building to some transcendent moment. I gravitate toward texts that attempt to show--and not just tell--about this feature of our existence. The reality, I believe, Kafka is proposing is that we aren't necessarily building to any logical apex of life or existence. We spin our wheels and then once we kick the bucket, the rest of us go on spinning, churning, grasping for some shred of meaning. Kafka had this all figured out. Amen.

B002DKF47O|5.0|Behemoth don't exactly break new ground on their ninth full-length, 2009's \\"Evangelion.\\" Sure, the record might make use of some Egyptian musicianship, orchestration, keyboards, trumpets, horns, trombones, and tubas, but it is far from being an experimental release like 2007's \\"Apostasy\\" was. Instead, for the most part, Behemoth just give the fans more of what they want, delivering truckloads of smoking riffs, pummeling blast beats, intricate leads, technical solos, and furious death metal bellows. As such, no matter how familiar it may sound, this album is hard for any metalhead to dislike. And besides, there is one aspect that is unique to \\"Evangelion,\\" and that is its fluidity -- the songs flow well into each other, thus producing seamless, wall-to-wall sequencing.<br /><br />\\"Daimonos\\" begins with a chilling, commanding, spoken-word intro before slamming into a brick wall of death-thrash with devastating blasts, scalding, Slayer-worthy thrash riffing, and rip-roaring rhythms. And the latter half of this song is highlighted by an excellent, lengthy, technically-impressive guitar solo. \\"Shemhamforash\\" works in similar fashion, beginning with a brief melodic intro before BAM!, you are smacked across the face by a full-on assault of head-spinning, blast beat-propelled black/death metal chaos. A pair of whipping and careening solos pops up, here, too, although the song does end on a restrained and nuanced note, with a splash of mysteriously colorful, epic-sounding Spanish-guitar strumming in the outro. \\"Ov Fire And The Void\\" begins as a mostly mid-tempo venture, with a martial, cascading drum solo, strong, chugging bass line, and ominous wall of feedback. Some chunky guitars and thumping drum beats come smashing in, but the song never really takes off, out of restrained territory and into brutal, full-on thrash territory, until about three-minutes in.<br /><br />\\"Transmigrating Beyond Realms Ov Amenti,\\" however, is a truly breakneck endeavor with blistering buzzsaw riffing, furious drumming, and bottom-of-the-gut growling. Inferno's drumming is really impressive in this song, as he shows off some very dexterous and thrashy fills; but the real highlight, here, is when the guitarists -- Nergal and Seth -- trade-off wild, shredding, screaming solos. \\"He Who Breeds Pestilence\\" begins on a relatively trippy note, with the sound of a few bird noises. Soon thereafter, though, it turns to punishing, hyper-speed picking and drumming. But the track does retain a certain melodic sensibility, as it does feature some seemingly innocent and docile guitar strumming and some nicely melodic -- if easy to overlook -- soloing in the outro. \\"The Seed Ov I\\" is backed by hefty, forceful, muscular rhythms, bottom-heavy chugging, and is also highlighted by a brief but cool, rolling drum solo, and two great, and fairly darn wailing guitar solos.<br /><br />\\"Alas, Lord Is Upon Me\\" is much like \\"The Seed...\\" in that it begins with a few booming opening power chords (and backing guitar harmonies), before gradually gaining momentum, and eventually hitting hyper-speed territory with chunky, steamrolling riffs and breakneck drumming. \\"Defiling Morality Ov Black God\\" is, essentially, a blast-fest from start to finish. It boils over with crushing, mind-boggling, and at-times \\"rat-tat-tat\\" machine-gun blasting. (Inferno's double kick work is truly blistering, here, and his snare-battery is virtuosic.) Lastly, if far from least, the album wraps up with \\"Lucifer,\\" a truly, bone-chillingly dark and ominous piece of straight-up, droning doom metal.<br /><br />In the end, Behemoth's songwriting may have stalled a bit, here, but their musical delivery is still top-notch. Every song explodes with enough convincing vigor and enthusiasm. As such, whether revving up the engines or settling down into a comparatively slow dirge, there is nary a single weak moment to be found anywhere on this album. Therefore, \\"Evangelion\\" might not bring anything really new or innovative to the table, but it nonetheless still makes for a very satisfying listen.o the table, but it nonetheless still makes for a very satisfying listen.
